Third Proof: Quranic Promise of Caliphate
Author cites Quran 24:55 as evidence for the caliphate of the four rightly guided caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 24:55 is used as a proof for the caliphate of the four rightly guided caliphs in order.

Core Idea
Quran 24:55 promises caliphate to believers; it was fulfilled in the four imams.

In this lesson, we examine the third proof for the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The author cites a Quranic promise of succession (istikhlāf) and argues that it was realized specifically in the four imams, in their historical order. This direct scriptural evidence is a key argument in Sunni political theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic verse and its translation carefully. Notice that the author quotes a verse and then gives an interpretation.
The verse is Quran 24:55.
2
Identify the proof's structure
The proof consists of a Quranic promise and an argument that it applies to the four caliphs. Identify the premise and conclusion.
3
Reflect on the restriction
Why does the author say 'it has not been established for others besides the four imams'? Consider the historical context.
The author relies on the fact that only these four ruled in succession after the Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - قوله تعالى : ( وعد الله الذين آمنوا منكم وعملوا الصالحات ليستخلفنهم في الأرض) (۱). وعد الخلافة لجماعة من المؤمنين المخاطبين، ولم يثبت لغير الائمة الأربعة، فيثبت لهم على الترتيب .
The third – His statement, exalted be He: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession [to authority] upon the earth' (Quran 24:55). He promised the caliphate to a group of the addressed believers, and it has not been established for others besides the four imams, so it is established for them in order.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof for the caliphate of Abu Bakr and the subsequent rightly guided caliphs. The author quotes Quran 24:55, in which God promises to grant succession (istikhlāf) to believers who have faith and do good deeds. He argues that this promise was fulfilled in the four imams (the Rightly Guided Caliphs: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) and not in anyone else. Therefore, the caliphate is established for them in order, meaning in the historical sequence in which they ruled. This is a direct scriptural proof from the Quran.

Key Terms
خلافة
استخلاف
آية
ائمة أربعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic promise of caliphate applies to all believers.
Correction: The author restricts it to the four rightly guided caliphs based on historical fulfillment.

Checkpoint
According to the author, who does the Quranic promise of caliphate in verse 24:55 apply to?
A) All believers
B) The four rightly guided caliphs in order
C) Only Ali
D) Only Abu Bakr

Key Takeaway
The promise of caliphate in Quran 24:55 was fulfilled specifically in the four rightly guided caliphs in order.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s promise in Quran 24:55 was fulfilled exactly for the four caliphs, do you believe that every promise Allah makes to believers is fulfilled precisely? Has your heart ever wavered waiting for a promise from Him? What would it take for you to trust His timing completely?
?
The author restricts a specific divine promise to four individuals. Does your veneration of the early caliphs match the weight of this evidence? Or do you unconsciously rank them lower than other figures? Search your heart: do you genuinely acknowledge their unique status as the fulfillment of this verse?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and being asked: Did you accept the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali as He willed? If you are hesitant, what in your soul resists? Commit today to learning more about their virtues until your heart is at peace with their rank.

The Mahdi and Jesus as Signs of the Hour: Orthodox Sunni View
Critique of Imami occultation and citation of Mahdi hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Mahdi and Jesus as signs of the Hour, and the critique of the Imami occultation claim based on hadith authenticity.

Core Idea
The Mahdi will appear from Fatima's lineage, but his occultation is rejected; authentic hadiths are ahad, not mutawatir.

This conclusion (khatima) of the author addresses two major eschatological figures: the Mahdi and Jesus. It affirms the authentic hadiths about the Mahdi from the Prophet's family, while sharply criticizing the Imami Shi'a doctrine that he has been hidden for centuries. The passage also clarifies the epistemological status of these hadiths (solitary reports) and distinguishes them from the mutawatir hadith on the Dajjal.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the author's flow: starting with the hadiths, critique, then the hadith citations and their status.
Notice the author uses 'خاتمة' (conclusion) setting this as a summary topic.
2
Identify the critique of Imami occultation
Find the sentence where the author rejects the Imami claim of the Mahdi's birth and hiding. Understand why he calls it 'ذهاب بلا حجة' (departure without proof).
The author links hiding (الاختفاء) only to Jesus' descent and Dajjal's emergence.
3
Examine the hadiths and their transmission
List the hadiths cited about the Mahdi. Note that the author says they are 'صحاح وإن كانت أحاداً' (sound, though solitary). Contrast with the Dajjal hadith which he says is 'متواتر المعنى' (mutawatir in meaning).
This is key for understanding the epistemological weight of these reports in creed.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the Mahdi is a just Imam from Fatima's descendants, created by Allah when He wills. This affirms the orthodox Sunni view against the Imami occultation.
The final footnote reinforces that ahad hadiths are not used for establishing creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : خاتمة
قد وردت الأحاديث الصحيحة في ظهور إمام من ولد فاطمة الزهراء (رضي الله عنها) يملأ الدنيا قسطاً وعدلا كما ملئت جوراً وظلماً وقول الإمامية أنه قد ولد واختفى ما فوق أربعمائة سنة خوفاً من الأعداء ذهاب بلا حجة إلى إمام بلا حكمة على أن الناس بعد بني العباس يطلبونه من السماء فما له. والاختفاء في نزول عيسى وخروج الدجال) .
مما يلحق بباب الإمامة بحث خروج المهدي، ونزول عيسى (صلى الله عليه وسلم) وهما امن أشراط الساعة . وقد وردت في هذا الباب أخبار صحاح، وإن كانت أحاداً. ويشبه أن يكون حديث خروج الدجال متواتر المعنى، أما خروج المهدي فعن ابن عباس الله (رضي عنه) أنه قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا تذهب الدنيا حتى يملك العرب رجل من أهل بيتي يواطىء اسمه اسمي .
وعن ابن سلمة قال سمعت رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) يقول : المهدي من عترتي من ولد فاطمة .
(
وعن أبي سعيد الخدري، قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «المهدي مني ، أجلى الجبهة ، أقنى الأنف، يملأ الأرض قسطاً وعدلاً كما ملئت ظلما وجوراً يملك سبع سنين» (۱) .
وعنه (رضي الله عنه قال : ذكر رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) بلاءً يصيب هذه الأمة حتى لا يجد الرجل ملجأ يلجأ إليه من الظلم فيبعث الله رجلا من عترتي ، فيملأ به الأرض قسطاً وعدلاً كما ملئت جوراً وظلماً . فذهب العلماء إلى أنه إمام عادل من ولد فاطمة رضي الله عنها) يخلقه الله تعالى متى شاء، ويبعثه نصرة لدينه .
(۱) هذه الأحاديث كلها أحاديث آحاد وأحاديث الآحاد لا يأخذ بها في إثبات العقائد، وراجع كتابنا المذاهب المعاصرة وموقف الإسلام منها طبعة لجيل».
He said: Conclusion. Sound hadiths have been reported about the appearance of an Imam from the descendants of Fatimah al-Zahra (may Allah be pleased with her) who will fill the earth with equity and justice just as it was filled with tyranny and injustice. And the statement of the Imamis that he has been born and hidden for over four hundred years out of fear of enemies is a departure without proof to an Imam without wisdom, given that people after the Abbasids seek him from the sky, but what is wrong with him? And hiding is for the descent of Jesus and the emergence of the Dajjal. Included in the chapter of Imamate is the discussion of the emergence of the Mahdi and the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him), both are among the signs of the Hour. Sound reports have been transmitted in this chapter, even if they are solitary. And it is likely that the hadith about the emergence of the Dajjal is mutawatir in meaning. As for the emergence of the Mahdi, it is from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The world will not end until a man from my household, whose name matches my name, rules over the Arabs.' And from Ibn Salamah, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'The Mahdi is from my progeny, from the descendants of Fatimah.' And from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The Mahdi is from me, with a prominent forehead, a high-bridged nose, he will fill the earth with equity and justice just as it was filled with tyranny and injustice; he will rule for seven years.' And from him (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned a calamity that will afflict this community until a man finds no refuge to take shelter from injustice, so Allah will send a man from my progeny, and through him fill the earth with equity and justice just as it was filled with tyranny and injustice. So the scholars held that he is a just Imam from the descendants of Fatimah (may Allah be pleased with her), whom Allah the Exalted creates whenever He wills, and sends to support His religion.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion (khatima) that addresses the eschatological figures of the Mahdi and Jesus. It begins by stating that authentic hadiths predict an Imam from Fatima's line who will establish justice. It then criticizes the Imami Shi'a claim that this Imam has already been born and hidden for over four hundred years, calling it an unfounded belief. The author asserts that hiding (ghayba) pertains to Jesus' descent and the Dajjal's emergence, not to the Mahdi. He then cites several hadiths about the Mahdi, noting they are sound but solitary (ahad), while the Dajjal's hadith is likely mutawatir in meaning. He concludes by affirming that the Mahdi is a just Imam from Fatima's descendants, created by Allah when He wills.

Correction: The hadiths are solitary (ahad) and sound; the Mahdi will appear in the future, and his occultation is not supported.

Key Takeaway
The Mahdi is a promised figure from Fatima's lineage; his hadiths are authentic but solitary, and the Imami occultation doctrine is unfounded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author calls the Imami occultation 'a departure without proof'. Are there any beliefs you hold about the end times that are based on weak or fabricated reports? How would you react if someone challenged you to provide the source?
?
If you truly believed the Mahdi could appear at any moment, how would your priorities change today? Are you living as if the Hour is near, or are you comfortable with the distance?

Signs of the Hour and the Virtue of Generations
Author warns against Dajjal and lists other signs of the Hour, then discusses virtue of generations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major signs of the Hour as listed by the author and the theological reflection on the relative virtue of earlier versus later generations.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's deception and many signs show the Hour's imminence, yet later believers may earn greater reward.

The Prophet warned us to avoid the Dajjal because of his powerful doubts. Then the author lists many other signs that signal the end of time. These signs also reveal the virtue of earlier generations, but the author explains that later generations might still surpass them in reward due to the difficulty of faith in corrupt times.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping to analyze. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall flow.
Notice the list of signs is quite detailed.
2
Examine the Dajjal warning
Focus on the opening warning about the Dajjal. Why does the Prophet advise staying away? What makes his deception so dangerous?
The phrase 'because of the doubts he stirs up' is key.
3
Identify the other signs
Go through the list of other signs mentioned after the Dajjal. Count them and note their variety—cosmic, moral, social.
There are at least eight distinct signs listed.
4
Understand the argument about generations
The author says these signs show the goodness of earlier generations in terms of reward. But he then quotes the rain hadith to show later generations could be better. Think about why he includes this nuance.
Consider how difficulty increases reward in this worldview.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال عليه السلام من سمع بالدجال فلينأ عنه ، فوالله إن الرجل ليأتيه وهو يحسب أنه مؤمن فيتبعه مما تبعث له من الشبهات. قال : وغير ذلك من الأشراط ، كدابة الأرض، ويأجوج ومأجوج، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ، والخسوف الثلاثة، وقلة العلم والأمانة، وكثرة الفسق والخيانة ، ورئاسة الفساق والأرذال ، وفرط ازدياد عدد النساء على الرجال، وإشفاء الإسلام على الزوال، وانقضاء النظام إلى الانحلال ، وهذا هو الشر الذي يتبين منه خيرية القرون السابقة بحسب كثرة الثواب أيضاً، ويكون عند غاية قرب الساعة وانقراض زمن التوبة والطاعة، فلا ينافي احتمال خيرية آخر الأمة على ما قال رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) «مثل أمتي مثل المطر لا يدري أوله خير أم آخره» ؟ بناء على احتمال أن يفضل مع طول العهد وفساد الزمان ثواب المعرفة والايقان والطاعة والإيمان، ثبت الله قلوبنا على الدين، ووفقنا لما يرضاه يوم الدين، إنه خير موفق ومعين وصلى الله على النبي محمد وآله الطاهرين وأصحابه أجمعين، والحمد لله رب العالمين).
And he (peace be upon him) said: Whoever hears of the Dajjal, let him keep away from him, for by Allah, a man will come to him thinking he is a believer but will follow him because of the doubts he stirs up. He said: And other signs: the Beast of the Earth, Gog and Magog, the rising of the sun from its west, the three sinkings, scarcity of knowledge and trustworthiness, abundance of wickedness and treachery, leadership of the wicked and the base, excessive increase of women over men, Islam nearing extinction, and the order disintegrating into chaos. And this is the evil through which the goodness of the earlier generations becomes evident also in terms of abundance of reward. And it occurs at the extreme proximity of the Hour and the termination of the time of repentance and obedience. So it does not contradict the possibility of the later part of this community being better, according to what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The example of my community is like the rain; it is not known whether its beginning is better or its end.' Based on the possibility that with length of time and corruption of the age, the reward of knowledge, certainty, obedience, and faith might be greater. May Allah make our hearts firm upon the religion and grant us success in what pleases Him on the Day of Judgment. Indeed, He is the best of granters of success and helpers. May Allah bless the Prophet Muhammad, his pure family, and all his companions. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.)
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage begins with a warning from the Prophet about the Dajjal: anyone who hears of him should stay far away, because he will deceive even those who think they are believers through the doubts he raises. Then the author lists other major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth, Gog and Magog, the rising of the sun from the west, three sinkings (east, west, and Arabia), scarcity of knowledge and trustworthiness, increase of wickedness and treachery, the rise of corrupt leaders, the great increase of women relative to men, the near extinction of Islam, and the collapse of order. The author then explains that this great evil actually shows the superiority of earlier generations, because they had less temptation and greater reward. However, this does not contradict the possibility that later generations may be better in terms of reward, as indicated by the hadith 'My community is like the rain...' because with corruption, the difficulty of remaining faithful increases, and thus the reward for knowledge, certainty, obedience, and faith may be greater. The passage concludes with a supplication for steadfastness.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Dajjal is the only major sign of the Hour, and later generations cannot be better than earlier ones.
Correction: The author lists many signs besides the Dajjal, and the rain hadith shows that later generations may surpass earlier ones in reward due to the difficulty of faith in corrupt times.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
This passage teaches that while signs of the Hour indicate the greatness of earlier times, later believers may achieve greater reward through steadfastness amidst corruption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Are you actually striving in an environment of corruption, or are you coasting on the assumption that you are already among the saved? What concrete step will you take this week to increase your certainty?
?
If the reward for faith is greater in times of widespread wickedness, does that comfort you or challenge you? Will you seek to maximize your reward by enduring hardship for the truth, or will you remain passive? Make a commitment now to one action that pleases Allah despite the opposition.

The Ten Major Signs of the Hour
Hudhayfa reports the ten signs before the Hour as listed by the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten major signs that must appear before the Hour as reported by Hudhayfa ibn Asid, and know which are the first to appear.

Core Idea
Ten signs must appear before the Hour, beginning with the sun rising from the west and the Beast.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) informed his Companions about ten specific signs that will precede the Day of Judgment. In this hadith narrated by Hudhayfa ibn Asid, he lists them and highlights the first two to occur. This lesson presents the hadith and its key points.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the context: the Prophet finds the Companions discussing the Hour.
2
Identify the Ten Signs
List each of the ten signs mentioned. Pay attention to the order they are given.
The signs are: smoke, Dajjal, Beast, sun rising from west, descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three sinkings, and fire from Yemen.
3
Note the First Two Signs
The Prophet specifies that the first signs to appear are the sun rising from the west and the emergence of the Beast. This shows a sequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أشراط الساعة عن حذيفة بن أسيد الغفاري قال : اطلع النبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم) علينا ونحن نتذاكر فقال : ما تذكرون؟ قلنا نذكر الساعة ، قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات فذكر الدخان والدجال، والدابة، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، ونزول عيسى بن مريم، ويأجوج ومأجوج ، وثلاثة خسوف خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم . وقال : إن أول الآيات خروجاً طلوع الشمس من مغربها، وخروج الدابة على الناس ضحى .
From the signs of the Hour: from Hudhayfa ibn Asid al-Ghifari, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) looked upon us while we were discussing and said: What are you talking about? We said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: It will not come until you see ten signs before it. Then he mentioned: the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that will come out from Yemen, driving the people to their gathering place. And he said: The first of the signs to appear is the rising of the sun from its west and the emergence of the Beast upon the people in the forenoon.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This is a hadith from Hudhayfa ibn Asid in which the Prophet enumerates ten major signs that must appear before the Hour. The Prophet found the Companions discussing the Hour and told them it will not occur until they see these signs: (1) the smoke (dukhan), (2) the Dajjal, (3) the Beast (dābba), (4) the sun rising from the west, (5) the descent of Jesus, (6) Gog and Magog, and (7-9) three sinkings (khusūf) in the east, west, and Arabian Peninsula, and finally (10) a fire from Yemen that drives people to their gathering place. The Prophet added that the first sign to appear is the sun rising from the west and the emergence of the Beast. This highlights the specific sequence and certainty of these events.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the ten signs are all equally well-known or that their order is fixed beyond the first two.
Correction: The hadith specifically states the first two signs are the sun rising from the west and the Beast, but does not give a fixed order for the remaining eight.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet gave ten specific signs that will precede the Hour, with the rising of the sun from the west and the emergence of the Beast being the first to occur.

?
The Beast will speak to each person and mark them. When your own deeds are presented to you on that Day, what single action from today will you wish you had done differently? Write it down now and commit to changing it starting tomorrow.

The Sun's Prostration and Rising from the West
Abu Dharr reports the hadith explaining the sun's prostration under the Throne and its eventual rising from the west.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic explanation of the sun's daily journey and its connection to the major sign of the Hour—the rising from the west.

Core Idea
The sun's journey is an act of obedience that will one day be commanded to reverse as a sign of the End.

In this lesson, we explore a profound hadith where the Prophet ﷺ reveals the unseen reality behind the sun's daily setting. Abu Dharr's narration teaches us that the sun prostrates under the Throne and seeks permission to rise again—until a time comes when it will be ordered to return from the west. This draws directly from a Qur'anic verse and reinforces the doctrine of divine control over creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith and Translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation to get the full narrative of the sun's journey and the prophecy.
Notice the question-and-answer format: the Prophet tests Abu Dharr's knowledge.
2
Identify the Stages of the Sun's Journey
Identify the sequence: sunset → prostration under the Throne → asking permission → being permitted → eventual rejection and command to rise from the west.
This is a cause-and-effect chain showing normalcy and then a disruption.
3
Connect to the Qur'anic Verse
See how the Prophet interprets 'mustaqarr' (resting place) as under the Throne, linking the hadith to Divine revelation.
The verse is Surah Ya-Sin 36:38.
4
Reflect on the Theological Significance
Understand that this hadith affirms Allah's absolute control over celestial bodies and serves as a sign of the Hour, increasing faith in the unseen.
It also warns against taking natural laws as independent—they are sustained by Allah's permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي ذر قال : قال رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) حین غربت الشمس: أتدري أين تذهب هذه؟ قلت: الله ورسوله أعلم قال : فإنها تذهب حتى تسجد تحت العرش، فتستأذن فيؤذن لها، ويوشك أن تسجد فلا يقبل منها وتستأذن فلا يؤذن لها، فيقال لها: ارجعي من حيث جئت فتطلع من مغربها . فذلك قوله تعالى : والشمس تجري لمستقر لها قال : مستقرها تحت العرش.
And from Abu Dharr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said when the sun set: Do you know where this goes? I said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: It goes until it prostrates under the Throne, and asks permission, and permission is given to it. And soon it will prostrate but it will not be accepted, and it will ask permission but will not be given it, and it will be said to it: Return from whence you came, and it will rise from its west. That is the saying of the Most High: 'And the sun runs to its resting place.' He said: Its resting place is under the Throne.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This hadith from Abu Dharr explains the daily journey of the sun. The Prophet asked if they knew where the sun goes after setting. Abu Dharr replied that Allah and His Messenger know best. The Prophet explained that the sun goes and prostrates under the Throne, then asks permission to rise again, and is permitted. However, near the end of time, its prostration will not be accepted, and it will be commanded to return from where it came, meaning it will rise from the west. The Prophet then connected this to the Quranic verse 'And the sun runs to its resting place,' interpreting the resting place (mustaqarr) as under the Throne. This shows that the sun's current path is due to divine permission, and the rising from the west will be a fundamental change in the natural order as a major sign of the Hour.

Key Terms
الشمس
السجود تحت العرش
المستقر
طلوع الشمس من مغربها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun literally prostrates like a human with limbs.
Correction: The prostration is a form of obedience and submission known to Allah, appropriate to the sun's nature, not a physical imitative act.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet say will happen to the sun's prostration near the end of time?
A) It will prostrate and be accepted as always.
B) It will prostrate but not be accepted, and its permission to rise will be denied.
C) It will stop prostrating altogether.
D) It will prostrate twice.

Key Takeaway
The sun's current obedience is a sign of Allah's power, and its future rising from the west will be a definitive sign of the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The sun prostrates every day without fail. When was the last time you deliberately prostrated in submission to the One who commands the sun? If you knew that tomorrow the sun might rise from the west, would you prostrate today differently?
?
You see the sun set each evening—a sign of its obedience. But one day, that obedience will be replaced by a command to return from the west. Are you living as if that day could be tomorrow? What would change if you truly believed that?
?
The sun asks permission to rise, and it is granted—until it won't be. You also ask Allah for guidance and life each day. What will happen when He no longer accepts your return? Are you using the time He has given you to return to Him before He commands you to a rising you cannot undo?

Loss of Knowledge and Moral Decay
Hadiths list social and moral decay signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadiths about the loss of knowledge, increase of ignorance, alcohol, gender imbalance, and neglect of trust as signs of the Hour.

Core Idea
Moral decay—ignorance, intoxication, and broken trust—are early signs of the Hour.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) described several social and moral changes that will precede the Day of Judgment. These include the disappearance of true knowledge, the spread of ignorance, widespread drinking, a drastic gender imbalance, and the neglect of trustworthiness. This lesson examines these signs as reported in authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith on knowledge and ignorance
Read the first hadith carefully. Note the five elements: lifting of knowledge, increase of ignorance, increase of alcohol consumption, fewer men, more women.
2
Understand the gender imbalance
The hadith says fifty women will have one caretaker. Reflect on the social implications.
3
Read the hadith on trust
Read the second hadith: when trust is neglected, await the Hour. Consider what 'trust' means here.
4
Ask: why are these signs important?
These signs indicate a breakdown of society and morality, which is a precursor to the final Hour.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال : إن من أشراط الساعة أن يرفع العلم، ويكثر الجهل، ويكثر شرب الخمر، ويقل الرجال، ويكثر النساء، حتى يكون لخمسين امرأة قيم واحد . وقال رسول الله ( ) : إذا ضيعت الأمانة فانتظر الساعة . وقال رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) : أول أشراط الساعة نار تحشر الناس من المشرق إلى المغرب . وقال : لا تقوم الساعة حتى تخرج نار من أرض الحجاز تضيء أعناق الإبل ببصری . وقال عليه السلام لا تقوم الساعة حتى يتقارب الزمان، فتكون السنة کالشهر والشهر كالجمعة وتكون الجمعة كاليوم ، ويكون اليوم كالساعة، وتكون الساعة كالصرمة بالنار. وقال (عليه السلام لا تقوم الساعة إلا على شرار الخلق .
And he said: Among the signs of the Hour is that knowledge will be lifted, ignorance will become widespread, drinking of alcohol will increase, men will become few, and women will become many, until fifty women will have one caretaker. And the Messenger of Allah ( ) said: When trust is neglected, then await the Hour. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The first of the signs of the Hour is a fire that will gather people from the east to the west. And he said: The Hour will not come until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz, illuminating the necks of camels in Busra. And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not come until time draws near, so that the year becomes like a month, and the month like a week, and the week like a day, and the day like an hour, and the hour like the burning of a palm frond. And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not come except upon the worst of creation.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage compiles several hadiths about minor signs of the Hour. First, knowledge will be lifted, ignorance widespread, alcohol consumption increases, and the gender imbalance becomes extreme so that one man may have to care for fifty women. Second, the neglect of trustworthiness is a sign. Third, a fire will gather people from east to west. Fourth, a fire from Hijaz will illuminate camel necks as far as Busra. Fifth, time will contract dramatically: a year feels like a month, a month like a week, a week like a day, a day like an hour, and an hour like the quick burning of a palm frond. Finally, the Hour will come only upon the worst of people. These signs indicate moral and social decay as well as supernatural events.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what extreme gender ratio is mentioned as a sign of the Hour?
A) For every man, fifty women
B) Fifty women will have one caretaker
C) Men will be fifty times more than women
D) Women will be half of men

Key Takeaway
Social and moral decay—loss of knowledge, rise of ignorance, alcohol, gender imbalance, and broken trust—are clear signs that the Hour is near.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in my life where I am neglecting the trust (amanah) that Allah has placed upon me? What practical step can I take today to fulfill a trust I have been ignoring?
?
The Prophet (ﷺ) warned that knowledge will be lifted. How am I actively seeking and preserving Islamic knowledge in my own life, and am I spreading it to others?
?
When I see the signs of moral decay—like the increase in alcohol or broken trust—do I become complacent or does it stir me to prepare for the meeting with my Lord? What change must I make now?

The Two Fires as Signs of the Hour
Two hadiths describe fire signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two hadiths about fires that will appear before the Hour: one gathering people from east to west, and another from Hijaz.

Core Idea
Two supernatural fires will appear as early signs preceding the Day of Judgment.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) mentioned two distinct fires that will occur as signs of the Hour. The first will gather people from the east to the west, while the second will emerge from the land of Hijaz and illuminate the necks of camels in Busra. This lesson explains these remarkable events.

Guided Path
1
Read the first fire hadith
Read: 'The first of the signs of the Hour is a fire that will gather people from the east to the west.' Note that it is described as the first sign.
2
Read the second fire hadith
Read: 'The Hour will not come until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz, illuminating the necks of camels in Busra.' Reflect on the distance between Hijaz and Busra.
3
Compare the two fires
Both are supernatural events. The first gathers people, the second provides light over a great distance. They are distinct signs.
4
Understand their significance
These fires are extraordinary occurrences that break the natural order, indicating the approach of the Hour.

Source Text

Fifth, time will contract dramatically: a year feels like a month, a month like a week, a week like a day, a day like an hour, and an hour like the quick burning of a palm frond. Checkpoint
According to the hadith, what is described as the first of the signs of the Hour?
A) A fire from Hijaz
B) A fire that gathers people from east to west
C) Loss of knowledge
D) The appearance of the Dajjal

Key Takeaway
Two extraordinary fires will appear as early signs: one gathering people across the earth, another lighting up the sky from Hijaz to Syria.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to see the light of the second fire tonight, would you be prepared to stand before Allah? What tangible step can you take today to ensure you are ready for the Hour, even if it seems far away?
?
The first fire will gather people from east to west. When you think about all of humanity being assembled, does your heart tremble with fear or feel indifference? Ask yourself: what is the one sin you keep delaying to repent from, knowing that these signs are real and the Hour is near?
?
The signs of the Hour are not mere stories—they are certainties that will come to pass. Have you ever truly let the reality of these signs change how you live your daily life? If not, what is holding you back from taking your faith more seriously starting now?

Time Contraction and the Worst of Creation
Two hadiths: time compression and the worst people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about the contraction of time and the hadith that the Hour will come upon the worst of people.

Core Idea
Time will seem to speed up drastically, and the Hour will only come when humanity has reached its moral lowest.

Among the minor signs of the Hour is a remarkable temporal phenomenon where time itself feels compressed: years become like months, months like weeks, weeks like days, days like hours, and hours like the quick burning of a palm frond. Additionally, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the Hour will only come upon the worst of creation. This lesson explores these final signs.

Guided Path
1
Read the time contraction hadith
Read the hadith describing the progressive shortening of time units. Notice the sequence: year → month → week → day → hour → burning of a palm frond.
2
Understand the metaphor
The burning of a palm frond is very quick. This illustrates how brief an hour will feel.
3
Read the worst of creation hadith
Read: 'The Hour will not come except upon the worst of creation.' Reflect on the moral condition of people at that time.
4
Connect the signs
Time contraction may be related to the spiritual decay of humanity. When people become corrupt, time feels accelerated.

Source Text

Key Takeaway
Time will perceptibly speed up, and the Hour will only come when humanity is at its most wicked.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the Hour will only come upon the worst of creation. If you look at your own heart honestly, do you see signs of that moral decay creeping in? What specific sin or attitude are you tolerating that you know you must uproot today?
?
Time is accelerating: the hadith says a year will feel like a month. How are you spending the 'compressed' moments you have left? Are you investing them in what truly matters for the eternal Hour, or are you letting them slip away in distraction?
?
The Prophet ﷺ warned that the Hour will not come until humanity reaches its lowest. Does that sober you about the state of the world? More importantly, does it move you to action—or do you feel helpless? What is one concrete step you can take this week to be among the best of creation, not the worst?

Prophetic Hadiths on the Signs of the Hour
Author compiles multiple hadiths on Ashrat al-Sa'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will become familiar with several authentic hadiths that describe the major signs of the Hour (Ashrat al-Sa'ah) as narrated by the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The Prophet described specific, tangible signs preceding the Hour.

Before exploring the theological principle of literal interpretation, the author first presents a collection of Prophetic hadiths detailing the signs of the Hour. These narrations cover cosmic events, social breakdown, and temporal distortions. Read them carefully to appreciate the concrete nature of these eschatological predictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths sequentially
Read each hadith in order, noting the variety of signs mentioned—from the sun's prostration under the Throne to the contraction of time.
The hadiths are cited from multiple companions and collectors.
2
Identify the different categories of signs
Group the signs into categories: cosmic events (sun rising from west, fire from Hijaz), social changes (loss of knowledge, increase of ignorance and wine-drinking), and temporal anomalies (contraction of time).
3
Notice the chain of transmission references
Observe that the author cites well-known hadith collections (Muslim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawood) to establish authenticity.
This is important for the later argument about reliability.
4
Reflect on the literal nature of these descriptions
Consider whether these events could be understood literally or require allegorical interpretation. This prepares you for the next lesson's conclusion.
The author will argue they are literally possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي ذر قال : قال رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) حین غربت الشمس: أتدري أين تذهب هذه؟ قلت: الله ورسوله أعلم قال : فإنها تذهب حتى تسجد تحت العرش، فتستأذن فيؤذن لها، ويوشك أن تسجد فلا يقبل منها وتستأذن فلا يؤذن لها، فيقال لها: ارجعي من حيث جئت فتطلع من مغربها . فذلك قوله تعالى : والشمس تجري لمستقر لها (١) قال : مستقرها تحت العرش. وقال : إن من أشراط الساعة أن يرفع العلم، ويكثر الجهل، ويكثر شرب الخمر، ويقل الرجال، ويكثر النساء، حتى يكون لخمسين امرأة قيم واحد (۲) . وقال رسول الله ( ) : إذا ضيعت الأمانة فانتظر الساعة . وقال رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) : أول أشراط الساعة نار تحشر الناس من المشرق إلى المغرب . وقال : لا تقوم الساعة حتى تخرج نار من أرض الحجاز تضيء أعناق الإبل ببصری (۳). وقال عليه السلام لا تقوم الساعة حتى يتقارب الزمان، فتكون السنة کالشهر والشهر كالجمعة وتكون الجمعة كاليوم ، ويكون اليوم كالساعة، وتكون الساعة كالصرمة بالنار. وقال (عليه السلام لا تقوم الساعة إلا على شرار الخلق . سريحة قال : اطلع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وذكره. ورواه أبو داود في الملاحم ۱۲، ومسلم في الفتن ۳۹ ، ٤۰ والترمذي في الفتن ۲۱ وأحمد بن حنبل في المسند ٤ : ٧،٦ (حلبي). (۱) سورة يس آية رقم ۳۸ . (۲) الحديث رواه الترمذي في كتاب الفتن باب ما جاء في أشراط الساعة ٢٢٠٥ - حدثنا محمود بن غيلان حدثنا النضر بن شميل، حدثنا شعبة عن قتادة عن أنس قال رسول الله - وذكره . قال الترمذي. هذا حديث حسن صحيح. (۳) الحديث رواه الإمام مسلم في كتاب الفتن وأشراط الساعة ١٤ باب لا تقوم الساعة حتى تخرج نار من أرض الحجاز ٤٢ - (۲۹۰۲) بسنده عن أبي هريرة - رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : وذكره . وفي حديث آخر: لا تقوم حتى لا يقال في الأرض الله الله (۱) . - وذكر في حديث آخر من علامات الساعة أن تظهر الأصوات في المساجد، وأن يسود القبيلة فاسقهم، وأن يكون زعيم القوم أرذلهم، وأن يكرم الرجل مخافة شره. وبالجملة ، فالأحاديث في هذا الباب كثيرة رواها العدول الثقاة وصححها المحدثون الأثبات ، ولا يمتنع حملها على ظواهرها عند أهل الشريعة لأن المعاني المذكورة أمور ممكنة عقلا
And from Abu Dharr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said when the sun set: Do you know where this goes? I said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: It goes until it prostrates under the Throne, then it asks permission and is permitted, and soon it will prostrate and will not be accepted, and it will ask permission and will not be permitted, and it will be said to it: Return from whence you came, and it will rise from its setting place. That is the saying of the Most High: 'And the sun runs to its resting place' (1) He said: Its resting place is under the Throne. And he said: Verily, among the signs of the Hour are that knowledge will be raised, ignorance will become abundant, drinking of wine will become abundant, men will become few, and women will become numerous, until there is one caretaker for fifty women. (2) And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When trust is lost, then await the Hour. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The first of the signs of the Hour is a fire that will gather the people from the east to the west. And he said: The Hour will not be established until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz that illuminates the necks of the camels at Busra. (3) And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not be established until time becomes contracted, so the year will be like a month, the month like a week, the week like a day, the day like an hour, and the hour like the burning of a palm branch. And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not be established except upon the worst of creation. Suraihah said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) looked out and mentioned it. And Abu Dawood narrated it in Al-Malahim 12, Muslim in Al-Fitan 39, 40, Al-Tirmidhi in Al-Fitan 21, and Ahmad bin Hanbal in Al-Musnad 4:7,6 (Halabi). (1) Surah Ya-Sin verse 38. (2) The hadith was narrated by Al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Al-Fitan, Chapter on What Has Come about the Signs of the Hour, 2205 - from Mahmud bin Ghailan... he said: This is a hasan sahih hadith. (3) The hadith was narrated by Imam Muslim in the Book of Al-Fitan and the Signs of the Hour, 14, Chapter: The Hour will not be established until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz, 42 (2902) from Abu Hurairah... And in another hadith: It will not be established until 'Allah, Allah' is not said on earth. (1) And it is mentioned in another hadith that among the signs of the Hour are that voices will appear in mosques, that the wicked of the tribe will become its leader, that the leader of the people will be the most vile of them, and that a man will be honored for fear of his evil. In summary, the hadiths on this topic are many, narrated by trustworthy upright narrators and authenticated by reliable hadith scholars, and it is not impossible according to the people of the Shari'ah to carry them upon their apparent meanings, because the mentioned matters are things possible according to reason.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of prophetic hadiths concerning the signs of the Hour (Ashrat al-Sa'ah) followed by a general affirmation of the permissibility of taking them literally. The author first narrates several hadiths: the hadith of Abu Dharr about the sun prostrating under the Throne and eventually rising from the west; a hadith listing the raising of knowledge, increase of ignorance and wine-drinking, scarcity of men, and abundance of women; a hadith about the loss of trust; a hadith about a fire gathering people; a hadith about a fire from Hijaz; a hadith about the contraction of time; and a hadith about the Hour coming only upon the worst of creation. Interspersed are editorial citations (e.g., 'Suraihah said') and references to hadith collections. The author then adds another hadith about 'Allah, Allah' not being said, and lists additional signs: voices in mosques, a wicked tribal leader, a vile community leader, and honoring a man for fear of his evil. After this compilation, the author concludes with a summary statement: these hadiths are numerous, narrated by trustworthy and authenticated scholars, and it is not problematic for the people of Shari'ah to interpret them according to their apparent meanings (zawahir), because the described events are rationally possible. This establishes the principle that eschatological reports should be taken literally unless reason dictates otherwise.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
العدول الثقاة
المحدثون الأثبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The burning of a palm branch
B) A day

D) The blink of an eye

Key Takeaway
The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave detailed, literal descriptions of events that will occur before the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the Hour will not come except upon the worst of creation. What if you were alive at that moment? Would you be counted among them? What would you need to change starting today?
?
The Prophet said knowledge will be raised and ignorance will spread. Are you actively seeking knowledge of the Deen daily, or are you letting ignorance settle into your life? What is one concrete step you will take to ensure you are not part of that ignorance?
?
Trust being lost is a sign. Think of the trusts you hold—your prayers, your family, your wealth. Are you betraying any of them? If the Hour were imminent, which trust would you be most ashamed to face? Commit to restoring it today.

Unseen Matters
intermediate
5 min
The Principle of Literal Interpretation of Eschatological Hadiths
Author affirms literal interpretation of Ashrat al-Sa'ah hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that hadiths about the signs of the Hour can be taken literally because their content is rationally possible and transmitted by reliable narrators.

Core Idea
Literal interpretation of eschatological hadiths is permissible when rationally possible.

After presenting numerous hadiths on the signs of the Hour, the author concludes with a crucial methodological statement. He asserts that these reports have been narrated by trustworthy transmitters and authenticated by leading hadith scholars. Moreover, he argues that nothing prevents taking them literally, since the events they describe are possible within reason. This lesson unpacks that claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding statement
Carefully read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Identify the three key claims: (1) the hadiths are numerous, (2) they are narrated by trustworthy (al-`udul al-thiqat) and authenticated, (3) they can be taken literally because their meanings are rationally possible.
2
Examine the condition: 'rationally possible'
The author says 'لا يمتنع حملها على ظواهرها' (it is not impossible to carry them on their apparent meanings) because the events are 'أمور ممكنة عقلاً' (things possible according to reason). Understand that this is a rejection of allegorical interpretation that would dismiss these events as merely symbolic.
Reason here does not override revelation but confirms its plausibility.
3
Relate to the previous hadiths
Recall the hadiths from the previous lesson: sun rising from west, fire, contraction of time. Ask yourself: Are these rationally possible? The author says yes.
This establishes a general principle for interpreting eschatological reports.
4
Appreciate the role of trustworthy transmitters
The author mentions 'العدول الثقاة' (trustworthy upright narrators) and 'المحدثون الأثبات' (reliable hadith scholars) to emphasize the authenticity of these reports. This counters any claim that the hadiths are weak or fabricated.
Authenticity and rational possibility together justify literal interpretation.

(۱) سورة يس آية رقم ۳۸ . (۲) الحديث رواه الترمذي في كتاب الفتن باب ما جاء في أشراط الساعة ٢٢٠٥ - حدثنا محمود بن غيلان حدثنا النضر بن شميل، حدثنا شعبة عن قتادة عن أنس قال رسول الله - وذكره . قال الترمذي. هذا حديث حسن صحيح. And from Abu Dharr, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said when the sun set: Do you know where this goes? I said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: It goes until it prostrates under the Throne, then it asks permission and is permitted, and soon it will prostrate and will not be accepted, and it will ask permission and will not be permitted, and it will be said to it: Return from whence you came, and it will rise from its setting place. That is the saying of the Most High: 'And the sun runs to its resting place' (1) He said: Its resting place is under the Throne. And he said: Verily, among the signs of the Hour are that knowledge will be raised, ignorance will become abundant, drinking of wine will become abundant, men will become few, and women will become numerous, until there is one caretaker for fifty women. (2) And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When trust is lost, then await the Hour. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The first of the signs of the Hour is a fire that will gather the people from the east to the west. And he said: The Hour will not be established until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz that illuminates the necks of the camels at Busra. (3) And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not be established until time becomes contracted, so the year will be like a month, the month like a week, the week like a day, the day like an hour, and the hour like the burning of a palm branch. And he (peace be upon him) said: The Hour will not be established except upon the worst of creation. Suraihah said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) looked out and mentioned it. And Abu Dawood narrated it in Al-Malahim 12, Muslim in Al-Fitan 39, 40, Al-Tirmidhi in Al-Fitan 21, and Ahmad bin Hanbal in Al-Musnad 4:7,6 (Halabi). (1) Surah Ya-Sin verse 38. (2) The hadith was narrated by Al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Al-Fitan, Chapter on What Has Come about the Signs of the Hour, 2205 - from Mahmud bin Ghailan... he said: This is a hasan sahih hadith. (3) The hadith was narrated by Imam Muslim in the Book of Al-Fitan and the Signs of the Hour, 14, Chapter: The Hour will not be established until a fire comes out from the land of Hijaz, 42 (2902) from Abu Hurairah... And in another hadith: It will not be established until 'Allah, Allah' is not said on earth. (1) And it is mentioned in another hadith that among the signs of the Hour are that voices will appear in mosques, that the wicked of the tribe will become its leader, that the leader of the people will be the most vile of them, and that a man will be honored for fear of his evil. In summary, the hadiths on this topic are many, narrated by trustworthy upright narrators and authenticated by reliable hadith scholars, and it is not impossible according to the people of the Shari'ah to carry them upon their apparent meanings, because the mentioned matters are things possible according to reason.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of prophetic hadiths concerning the signs of the Hour (Ashrat al-Sa'ah) followed by a general affirmation of the permissibility of taking them literally. The author first narrates several hadiths: the hadith of Abu Dharr about the sun prostrating under the Throne and eventually rising from the west; a hadith listing the raising of knowledge, increase of ignorance and wine-drinking, scarcity of men, and abundance of women; a hadith about the loss of trust; a hadith about a fire gathering people; a hadith about a fire from Hijaz; a hadith about the contraction of time; and a hadith about the Hour coming only upon the worst of creation. Interspersed are editorial citations (e.g., 'Suraihah said') and references to hadith collections. The author then adds another hadith about 'Allah, Allah' not being said, and lists additional signs: voices in mosques, a wicked tribal leader, a vile community leader, and honoring a man for fear of his evil. After this compilation, the author concludes with a summary statement: these hadiths are numerous, narrated by trustworthy and authenticated scholars, and it is not problematic for the people of Shari'ah to interpret them according to their apparent meanings (zawahir), because the described events are rationally possible. This establishes the principle that eschatological reports should be taken literally unless reason dictates otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that supernatural eschatological events must be interpreted allegorically because they seem impossible.
Correction: The author argues that these events are rationally possible (possible 'aqlan) and therefore can be taken literally; allegorical interpretation is not required.

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the author gives for allowing literal interpretation of these hadiths?
A) They are narrated by many people
B) Their content is rationally possible
C) They are found in the Quran
D) They are approved by all scholars

Key Takeaway
Authentic hadiths about the Hour can be taken literally as long as their content is rationally possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the sun rising from the West or other signs of the Hour, do you truly accept them as literal future events, or does your heart lean toward metaphor? What does your response reveal about your trust in divine revelation?
?
The author bases literal interpretation on rational possibility. Have you ever dismissed a hadith about the Last Day as 'symbolic' simply because it seemed extraordinary? How does this lesson call you to reexamine that assumption?
?
These hadiths are authenticated by reliable narrators. Are you willing to order your life around the reality of these events, treating them as imminent rather than distant tales? What specific sign would you struggle to accept literally, and why?

Signs of the Hour: Literal vs Allegorical Interpretation
Lists hadiths on Hour signs, then discusses literal and allegorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key signs of the Hour mentioned in authentic hadiths and the methodological principle of interpreting them literally unless rationally impossible.

Core Idea
Eschatological hadiths are best understood literally unless rationally impossible.

This lesson introduces several authentic hadiths about the signs of the Hour and discusses the principle of literal interpretation. The author emphasizes that these signs are rationally possible and thus should be taken at face value, while also noting the allegorical interpretations offered by philosophers and some scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the overall content.
Pay attention to the list of signs and the shift to interpretation discussion.
2
Identify the signs of the Hour
From the hadiths mentioned, list the specific signs: disappearance of 'Allah, Allah', voices in mosques, rule of the wicked, leadership of the vilest, honoring evil men.
These are rationally possible events according to the author.
3
Understand the author's stance on interpretation
Notice that the author insists on literal interpretation (ẓawāhir) for these hadiths, and then presents allegorical interpretations by philosophers and some scholars for signs like the sun rising from the west, the fire from Hijaz, etc.
The author himself does not endorse allegory; he reports it.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حديث آخر: لا تقوم حتى لا يقال في الأرض الله الله. - وذكر في حديث آخر من علامات الساعة أن تظهر الأصوات في المساجد، وأن يسود القبيلة فاسقهم، وأن يكون زعيم القوم أرذلهم، وأن يكرم الرجل مخافة شره. وبالجملة، فالأحاديث في هذا الباب كثيرة رواها العدول الثقاة وصححها المحدثون الأثبات، ولا يمتنع حملها على ظواهرها عند أهل الشريعة لأن المعاني المذكورة أمور ممكنة عقلا وزعمت الفلاسفة أن طلوع الشمس من مغربها مما يجب تأويله بانعكاس الأمور وجريانها على غير ما ينبغي. وأول بعض العلماء النار الخارجة من الحجاز بالعلم والهداية، سيما الفقه الحجازي، والنار الحاشرة للناس بفتنة الأتراك، وخروج الدجال بظهور الشر والفساد، ونزول عيسى عليه السلام باندفاع ذلك وبدو الخير والصلاح، وتقارب الزمان بقلة الخير والبركة وذهاب فائدة الأيام والأوقات، أو بكثرة الغفلة والاشتغال بأمر الدنيا ولذاتها، وبحدوث الفتن العظام الشاغلة لقلوب الأنام عما يمضي عليهم من الليالي والأيام.
And in another hadith: 'The Hour will not be established until 'Allah, Allah' is not said on the earth.' And it is mentioned in another hadith among the signs of the Hour: that voices will appear in the mosques, that the wicked of the tribe will rule, that the vilest of the people will become their leader, and that a man will be honored for fear of his evil. In summary, the hadiths on this topic are many, narrated by trustworthy and reliable narrators, and authenticated by established hadith scholars. It is not objectionable to take them according to their apparent meanings for the people of the Sharia, because the mentioned meanings are rationally possible. The philosophers claimed that the rising of the sun from its west must be interpreted allegorically as the reversal of affairs and their running contrary to what is proper. Some scholars interpreted the fire emerging from the Hijaz as knowledge and guidance, especially Hijazi jurisprudence; the fire that gathers people as the turmoil of the Turks; the emergence of the Dajjal as the appearance of evil and corruption; the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, as the repulsion of that and the emergence of good and righteousness; the shortening of time as the scarcity of good and blessing and the loss of benefit of days and times, or as abundant heedlessness and preoccupation with worldly affairs and pleasures; and the occurrence of great tribulations that occupy the hearts of people from what passes over them of nights and days.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage enumerates several hadiths about the signs of the Hour, then discusses the principle of literal interpretation. The author first lists hadithic signs: the disappearance of the declaration of 'Allah, Allah' from the earth, voices in mosques, the rule of the wicked, the leadership of the vilest, and honoring people out of fear. He emphasizes that these hadiths are authentic and should be understood literally because their meanings are rationally possible. He then mentions that the philosophers allegorize the sun rising from the west as a metaphor for chaotic reversal. The author also reports that some scholars offer allegorical interpretations for other signs: the fire from Hijaz as knowledge, the gathering fire as Turkish turmoil, the Dajjal as evil, Jesus' descent as restoration of good, shortening time as loss of blessings or increased heedlessness, and great tribulations as distractions. The passage thus shows the author's commitment to literal interpretation while acknowledging alternative views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that all eschatological hadiths must be interpreted metaphorically.
Correction: The author insists that these hadiths should be understood literally unless the meaning is rationally impossible, as they are narrated by trustworthy sources and describe possible events.

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary stance on interpreting hadiths about the signs of the Hour?
A) They must all be interpreted allegorically.
B) They should be taken literally unless impossible.
C) Only the philosophers' interpretations are valid.
D) They have no application to real events.

Key Takeaway
Signs of the Hour in authentic hadiths should be understood literally as rationally possible events, not forced into allegory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Nature and Origin of Gog and Magog
Describes the origin, physical traits, and numbers of Gog and Magog, and the construction of the barrier.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the origins, physical descriptions, and the initial barrier built against Gog and Magog.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are a vast, destructive multitude sealed behind a barrier.

This lesson introduces Gog and Magog as described in Islamic eschatology. We will explore their lineage, their extraordinary numbers, and their varied physical forms, as well as the reason Dhul-Qarnayn built a barrier to contain them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about Gog and Magog
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Note the two opinions on their origin.
The passage mentions two possibilities: from Japheth or from Adam.
2
Understand their numbers and sizes
Notice the claim that each man sees a thousand male offspring, and the extreme heights (50 or 120 cubits) and some are very short.
3
Learn about their destructive behavior
They attacked righteous people, destroying crops and livestock. This led Dhul-Qarnayn to build a barrier.
The barrier is a key element in their story.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما يأجوج ومأجوج فقيل: من أولاد يافث بن نوح، وقيل: جمع كثير من أولاد آدم أضعاف سائر بني آدم، لأنه لا يموت الرجل منهم حتى ينظر إلى ألف ذكر من صلبه، يحملون السلاح، فمنهم من هو في غاية الطول خمسون ذراعاً، وقيل: مائة وعشرون ذراعاً، ومنهم من طوله وعرضه كذلك، ومنهم من هو في غاية القصر، كانوا يخرجون إلى قوم صالحين بقربهم، فيهلكون زروعهم وضروعهم ويقتلونهم. فجعل ذو القرنين سداً دونهم، فيحفرون كل يوم السد حتى إذا كادوا يرون شعاع الشمس، قال الذي عليهم: ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً، فيعيده الله كما كان، حتى إذا بلغت مدتهم حفروا حتى إذا كادوا يرون شعاع الشمس، قال الذي عليهم: ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً إن شاء الله فيعودون وهو كهيئته فيحفرونه ويخرجون مقدمتهم بالشام وساقتهم بخراسان فيشربون المياه، وينحصر الناس منهم في حصونهم، ولا يقدرون على إتيان مكة والمدينة وبيت المقدس، فيرسل الله عليهم في أمعائهم فيهلكون جميعاً، فيرسل طيراً فيلقيهم في البحر، ويرسل مطراً فيغسل الأرض. وخروجهم يكون بعد خروج الدجال وقتل عيسى إياه.
As for Gog and Magog, it is said: they are from the children of Japheth son of Noah, and it is said: a great multitude from the children of Adam, many times the rest of mankind, because a man among them does not die until he sees a thousand male offspring from his loins, carrying weapons. Among them are some of extreme height, fifty cubits, and it is said: one hundred and twenty cubits; and among them are those whose length and width are like that; and among them are some of extreme shortness. They used to go out to righteous people near them, destroying their crops and livestock and killing them. So Dhul-Qarnayn built a barrier against them. Every day they dig at the barrier until they almost see the sun's rays, then the one in charge says: 'Go back, you will dig it tomorrow.' Then God restores it as it was. When their appointed time comes, they dig until they almost see the sun's rays, then the one in charge says: 'Go back, you will dig it tomorrow, God willing.' Then they return to find it as it was, then they dig and break through. Their vanguard reaches Syria and their rearguard is in Khorasan. They drink up the waters, and people take refuge from them in their fortresses. They cannot approach Mecca, Medina, and Jerusalem. Then God sends worms in their necks and they all die. Then God sends birds that cast them into the sea, and sends rain that cleanses the earth. Their emergence occurs after the emergence of the Dajjal and the killing of him by Jesus.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed description of Gog and Magog (Yajuj and Majuj). The author presents two accounts of their origin: some say they are descendants of Japheth son of Noah, others say they are a vast multitude from the children of Adam. Their enormous numbers are illustrated by the fact that every man among them sees a thousand male offspring before dying. They vary greatly in size, some extremely tall (up to 120 cubits) and some extremely short. Their destructive nature is shown by their habit of attacking righteous neighbors, destroying crops and livestock and killing people. The story of Dhul-Qarnayn's barrier is recounted: every day they try to dig through, but each night God restores it. This continues until their appointed time, when they succeed by saying 'God willing.' They then flood out, covering the region from Syria to Khorasan, drinking all water and besieging people. However, God destroys them by sending worms in their necks, then birds carry them to the sea, and rain cleans the earth. Their emergence is timed after the Dajjal and the killing of the Dajjal by Jesus.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
ذو القرنين
سد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Gog and Magog are purely metaphorical or symbolic.
Correction: The passage describes them as real physical beings with specific origins, sizes, and actions, indicating they are literal.

Checkpoint

C) From the children of Ham
D) From the children of Ishmael

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog are a real, numerous, and destructive people sealed by Dhul-Qarnayn's barrier.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that Gog and Magog are a multitude beyond imagination, destined to cause immense destruction. How does this truth challenge your daily priorities? Will you commit today to ask Allah for refuge from the trials of this world and the next?
?
The passage describes Gog and Magog destroying crops and killing righteous people. Is there any destructive pattern in your own life—words, habits, or negligence—that harms your neighbors? What is one concrete barrier you will build this week to stop it?
?
The barrier built by Dhul-Qarnayn was a physical structure. What spiritual barrier have you constructed to protect your faith from the 'Gog and Magog' of societal pressures and distractions? If none, what step will you take today to start building one?

The Breakthrough and Destruction of Gog and Magog
Describes the digging, breakthrough, destruction of Gog and Magog, and timing relative to Dajjal and Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Gog and Magog will break the barrier, their rampage, their destruction by God, and the timing of their emergence after Dajjal and Jesus.

Core Idea
God will destroy Gog and Magog in a miraculous way after they break the barrier.

This lesson continues the story of Gog and Magog, focusing on their eventual breakthrough from the barrier, the devastation they cause, and the divine intervention that destroys them. We will also see when this event occurs in the end times sequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the digging process
Notice the daily digging and restoration of the barrier until the appointed time when they say 'In sha Allah' and succeed.
The phrase 'إن شاء الله' is crucial for their breakthrough.
2
Understand their rampage and limits
They cover from Syria to Khorasan, drink water, but cannot enter Mecca, Medina, and Jerusalem.
This shows divine protection of sacred places.
3
Learn about their destruction
God sends worms in their necks, then birds carry them to the sea, and rain cleans the earth.
4
Note the timing
Their emergence is after Dajjal and Jesus killing the Dajjal.
This sequences the end times events.

وأما يأجوج ومأجوج فقيل: من أولاد يافث بن نوح، وقيل: جمع كثير من أولاد آدم أضعاف سائر بني آدم، لأنه لا يموت الرجل منهم حتى ينظر إلى ألف ذكر من صلبه، يحملون السلاح، فمنهم من هو في غاية الطول خمسون ذراعاً، وقيل: مائة وعشرون ذراعاً، ومنهم من طوله وعرضه كذلك، ومنهم من هو في غاية القصر، كانوا يخرجون إلى قوم صالحين بقربهم، فيهلكون زروعهم وضروعهم ويقتلونهم. فجعل ذو القرنين سداً دونهم، فيحفرون كل يوم السد حتى إذا كادوا يرون شعاع الشمس، قال الذي عليهم: ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً، فيعيده الله كما كان، حتى إذا بلغت مدتهم حفروا حتى إذا كادوا يرون شعاع الشمس، قال الذي عليهم: ارجعوا فستحفرونه غداً إن شاء الله فيعودون وهو كهيئته فيحفرونه ويخرجون مقدمتهم بالشام وساقتهم بخراسان فيشربون المياه، وينحصر الناس منهم في حصونهم، ولا يقدرون على إتيان مكة والمدينة وبيت المقدس، فيرسل الله عليهم في أمعائهم فيهلكون جميعاً، فيرسل طيراً فيلقيهم في البحر، ويرسل مطراً فيغسل الأرض. وخروجهم يكون بعد خروج الدجال وقتل عيسى إياه.
As for Gog and Magog, it is said: they are from the children of Japheth son of Noah, and it is said: a great multitude from the children of Adam, many times the rest of mankind, because a man among them does not die until he sees a thousand male offspring from his loins, carrying weapons. Among them are some of extreme height, fifty cubits, and it is said: one hundred and twenty cubits; and among them are those whose length and width are like that; and among them are some of extreme shortness. They used to go out to righteous people near them, destroying their crops and livestock and killing them. So Dhul-Qarnayn built a barrier against them. Every day they dig at the barrier until they almost see the sun's rays, then the one in charge says: 'Go back, you will dig it tomorrow.' Then God restores it as it was. When their appointed time comes, they dig until they almost see the sun's rays, then the one in charge says: 'Go back, you will dig it tomorrow, God willing.' Then they return to find it as it was, then they dig and break through. Their vanguard reaches Syria and their rearguard is in Khorasan. They drink up the waters, and people take refuge from them in their fortresses. They cannot approach Mecca, Medina, and Jerusalem. Then God sends worms in their necks and they all die. Then God sends birds that cast them into the sea, and sends rain that cleanses the earth. Their emergence occurs after the emergence of the Dajjal and the killing of him by Jesus.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed description of Gog and Magog (Yajuj and Majuj). The author presents two accounts of their origin: some say they are descendants of Japheth son of Noah, others say they are a vast multitude from the children of Adam. Their enormous numbers are illustrated by the fact that every man among them sees a thousand male offspring before dying. They vary greatly in size, some extremely tall (up to 120 cubits) and some extremely short. Their destructive nature is shown by their habit of attacking righteous neighbors, destroying crops and livestock and killing people. The story of Dhul-Qarnayn's barrier is recounted: every day they try to dig through, but each night God restores it. This continues until their appointed time, when they succeed by saying 'God willing.' They then flood out, covering the region from Syria to Khorasan, drinking all water and besieging people. However, God destroys them by sending worms in their necks, then birds carry them to the sea, and rain cleans the earth. Their emergence is timed after the Dajjal and the killing of the Dajjal by Jesus.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
ذو القرنين
سد
الدجال
عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Gog and Magog will be destroyed by human armies or natural causes.
Correction: The passage states their destruction is entirely divine: worms, birds, and rain.

Checkpoint
What happens when Gog and Magog finally break through the barrier?
A) They are immediately destroyed by fire from the sky.
B) They spread from Syria to Khorasan but cannot enter Mecca, Medina, and Jerusalem.
C) They conquer all of Arabia and destroy the Kaaba.
D) They follow the Dajjal and rule for forty days.

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog will break the barrier, cause widespread destruction, but be miraculously destroyed by God, occurring after Dajjal and Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the leader of Gog and Magog said 'God willing' after so many failed attempts, God allowed the breakthrough. Do you attach 'Insha'Allah' to your plans out of habit, or with genuine reliance on Allah's will? What would change if you meant it from the heart?
?
Despite the overwhelming destruction of Gog and Magog, they could not even approach Mecca, Medina, or Jerusalem. Where is your ultimate refuge? Are you seeking protection in fortresses of your own making, or in the protection of Allah that no force can overcome?
?
God destroyed Gog and Magog through tiny worms in their intestines—an unseen, humble cause. Do you truly believe that Allah can defeat the greatest evils with the smallest means? How does that shape your hope when you face seemingly insurmountable challenges?
