Objection to Last Generation Being Worst
Objection and answer focusing on the extreme end times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith-based objection about the last generation being the worst and how the answer distinguishes the very end of the world from earlier end times.

Core Idea
The evil of the last generation applies only just before the Hour, not to all end times.

This passage begins with a potential contradiction: some hadiths say the community’s last generation is evil, while a famous hadith compares the community to rain, uncertain which part is better. The author resolves this by pointing to a specific eschatological scenario—the final moments before the Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Start by reading the objection that certain hadiths suggest the last generation is the worst of creation, contrasting with the rain hadith that leaves uncertainty.
The objection is introduced with 'فإن قيل'.
2
Identify the answer's core
Notice the author immediately responds with 'قلنا: الشرارة الظاهرة...' indicating that the extreme wickedness is limited to the very approach of the Hour.
3
Examine the first scenario
Read the detailed description of events just before the Hour: Jesus kills the Dajjal, then a wind takes all believers, leaving the worst people who worship idols.
This is the scenario where the last generation is indeed evil.
4
Understand the temporal limit
Recognize that the author uses this scenario to show that the 'worst generation' refers only to the time when obligation ends, not the entire end times.
The hadith about the Hour not being established on anyone saying 'Allah' confirms this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: بعض هذه الأحاديث يشعر بأن الأمة في آخر الزمان شر الخلق قليل الخير، وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: مثل أمتي مثل المطر، لا يدري أوله خير آخره. قلنا: الشرارة الظاهرة التي لا شك معها في خيرية القرون السابقة إنما هي عند غاية قرب الساعة، وحين انقراض زمن التكليف أو كاد على ما ورد في الحديث أنه يمكث عيسى بن مريم في الناس بعد قتل الدجال سبع سنين، ليس اثنين عداوة، ثم يرسل الله ريحا باردة من قبل الشام فلا يبقى على وجه الأرض أحد في قلبه مثقال ذرة من خير أو إيمان إلا قبضته، ويبقى شرار الناس في خفة الطير وأحلام السباع لا يعرفون معروفاً ولا ينكرون منكراً، فيأمرهم الشيطان بعبادة الأوثان، وهم في ذلك دار رزقهم حسن عيشهم، ثم ينفخ في الصور. وهذا ما قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا تقوم الساعة على أحد يقول: الله الله. وأما في آخر الزمان عند كون الأمة في الجملة على الطاعة والإيمان، فلا يبعد كونهم خيراً عند الله وأكثر ثواباً باعتبار انقيادهم وإيمانهم مع الغيبة عن مشاهدة نزول الوحي وظهور المعجزات وهبوط الخيرات والبركات، وباعتبار ثباتهم على الإيمان والطاعات والعلوم والمعارف، وإرشاد الطوائف مع الزمان وشيوع المنكرات وكساد الفضائل، ورواج الرذائل، واستيلاء أهل الفساد.
If it is said: Some of these hadiths suggest that the community in the end times is the worst of creation, having little good, while the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The likeness of my community is that of rain; one does not know whether its beginning is better or its end.' We say: The apparent wickedness regarding which there is no doubt of the superiority of earlier centuries exists only at the extreme approach of the Hour, and at the time of the end of the period of obligation or nearly so, according to the hadith that Jesus son of Mary will remain among the people after killing the Dajjal for seven years, there being no enmity between two people. Then God will send a cold wind from the direction of Syria, and it will not leave anyone on the face of the earth having in his heart a mustard grain of good or faith without taking him. Then the worst of people will remain, in lightness of birds and dreams of predators, not knowing good nor forbidding evil. Then Satan will command them to worship idols, and they, in that state, will have abundant provision and a good life. Then the trumpet will be blown. And this is what the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The Hour will not be established upon anyone who says: Allah, Allah.' As for the end times when the community as a whole is upon obedience and faith, it is not far that they are better in the sight of God and more rewardable, considering their compliance and faith despite absence of witnessing revelation, miracles, and blessings, and considering their steadfastness in faith, obedience, knowledge, and guidance of groups despite the prevalence of evils, scarcity of virtues, spread of vices, and dominance of corrupt people.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: some hadiths seem to indicate that the end-time community is the worst, while another hadith compares the community to rain, uncertain whether the first or last is better. The author replies by distinguishing two phases. The first phase is just before the Hour, when obligation ends: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, there will be seven years of peace, then a wind takes all believers, leaving only the worst people who are like beasts, worship idols, and live well. On these the Hour will come. But the second phase is the general end times when the community is still on obedience and faith. In that case, they may be better and more rewarded because they remain steadfast despite not seeing miracles or prophets, and despite widespread corruption. Thus the apparent contradiction is resolved by temporal distinction.

Key Terms
آخر الزمان
شَرّ الخلْق
التكليف
عيسى
الدجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All end times are evil and the last generation is always the worst.
Correction: The extreme evil is only at the very last moment before the Hour, not the entire period of the end times.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the extreme wickedness of the last generation occur?
A) Throughout the entire end times
B) Only at the extreme approach of the Hour when obligation ends
C) After the Resurrection
D) During the reign of the Dajjal

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction is resolved by limiting the 'worst generation' to the final moments before the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The cold wind will take everyone with even a mustard grain of faith. If that wind came today, would you be taken or left behind? What does that reveal about the state of your heart right now?
?
After the believers are removed, the worst people live comfortably and worship idols without conscience. Are there any comforts or distractions in your life that have already numbed your sense of good and evil?
?
The Hour will not come upon anyone saying 'Allah'. Do you say 'Allah' with your tongue while your heart is attached to something else? What would it take for you to be among those who are taken by the wind, not left behind?

Last Generation Potentially Better
Explains why the last generation can be better in a different end-time context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the last generation can be considered better in God's sight due to their steadfast faith despite the absence of miracles and prevalence of corruption.

Core Idea
Faith without miracles is more rewarding than faith with them.

Having clarified that the extreme evil scenario is limited to just before the Hour, the author now turns to the general end times. Here, the community remains obedient and faithful, making them potentially superior to earlier generations precisely because of the difficulty of their circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Read the second scenario
Read the passage starting with 'وأما في آخر الزمان' which describes a different situation where the community is generally obedient.
2
Identify the reasons for superiority
Notice the factors listed: their compliance and faith despite absence of miracles, steadfastness, patience in teaching, and perseverance in a corrupt environment.
These are mentioned as 'باعتبار انقيادهم وإيمانهم مع الغيبة...' and 'باعتبار ثباتهم...'
3
Understand the resolution
Recognize that this second scenario shows the last generation can be better, resolving the earlier contradiction.
The key is that the hadith about being worst applies only to the first scenario, not this one.

?

Answering the Objection about the End-Time Ummah's Evil
The author answers the objection that the end-time ummah is evil with a distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author resolves the apparent contradiction between hadiths describing the end-time ummah as evil and those praising the later generations by distinguishing between the extreme end of time and the general end time.

Core Idea
The end-time ummah is not universally evil; evil is only at the extreme end when belief is taken away.

The objector points to hadiths that seem to show the later generation is evil, while other hadiths praise them. The author provides a careful answer by distinguishing two distinct periods in the end time. This passage is a classic example of reconciling apparently conflicting textual evidence through temporal differentiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the opening lines to understand the objector's claim: some hadiths suggest the end-time ummah is evil, and they cite the rain hadith.
Notice how the objection uses two seemingly contradictory hadiths.
2
Understand the distinction
The author distinguishes between the extreme nearness of the Hour and the general end time. Find where he explains the conditions of the extreme end (after Jesus kills the Dajjal, a cold wind takes believers, leaving only evil people).
This is the key to the answer.
3
Note the reconciliation
The author then argues that in the general end time (when the ummah is still upon obedience), they can be superior in reward due to their faith without witnessing miracles and their steadfastness despite corruption. He also reconciles with the best generations hadith.
The earlier generations are superior in quantity of worship and purity, not necessarily in reward for faith under hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : بعض هذه الأحاديث يشعر بأن الأمة في آخر الزمان شر الخلق قليل الخير ، وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ) : مثل أمتي مثل المطر، لا يدري أوله خير آخره (۱). قلنا : الشرارة الظاهرة التي لا شك معها في خيرية القرون السابقة إنما هي عند غاية قرب الساعة، وحين انقراض زمن التكليف أو كاد على ما ورد في الحديث أنه يمكث عيسى بن مريم في الناس بعد قتل الدجال سبع سنين، ليس [؟] عداوة، ثم يرسل الله ريحا باردة من قبل الشام فلا يبقى على وجه بين الأرض أحد في قلبه مثقال ذرة من خير أو إيمان(۲) إلا قبضته، ويبقى شرار الناس في خفة الطير وأحلام السباع لا يعرفون معروفاً ولا ينكرون منكراً، فيأمرهم الشيطان بعبادة الأوثان، وهم في ذلك دَار رزقهم حسن عيشهم، ثم ينفخ في الصور. وهذا ما قال ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) : « لا تقوم الساعة على أحد يقول : الله الله (۳) وأما في آخر الزمان عند كون الأمة في الجملة على الطاعة والإيمان، فلا يبعد كونهم خيراً عند الله وأكثر ثواباً باعتبار انقيادهم وإيمانهم مع الغيبة عن مشاهدة نزول الوحي وظهور المعجزات وهبوط الخيرات والبركات، وباعتبار ثباتهم على الإيمان والطاعات والعلوم والمعارف، وإرشاد الطوائف مع الزمان وشيوع المنكرات وكساد الفضائل، ورواج الرذائل، واستيلاء أهل الجهل والعناد والشر والفساد. وهذا لا ينافي خيرية القرون الأولى ومن يليهم بكثرة الطاعات والعبادات وصفاء العقائد وخلوص النيات، وقرب العهد بالنبي (صلى الله عليه وسلم ) وأصحابه، ونحو ذلك على ما قال ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) : « خير القرون القرن الذي أنا فيهم، ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ، ثم يفشو الكذب (۱) .
If it is said: Some of these hadiths indicate that the ummah at the end of time is the worst of creation, little in goodness, while the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The likeness of my ummah is that of rain; one does not know if its beginning is better or its end.' We say: The manifest evil concerning which there is no doubt about the goodness of the previous centuries is only at the extreme nearness of the Hour, and at the time of the extinction of the period of obligation or nearly so, as is related in the hadith that Jesus son of Mary will remain among the people after killing the Dajjal for seven years, not [؟] enmity, then Allah will send a cold wind from the direction of Syria, and there will not remain on the face of the earth anyone in whose heart is the weight of a mustard seed of good or faith except that it will seize him. And the worst of people will remain, in the lightness of birds and the intellects of beasts, not knowing good nor forbidding evil. Satan will order them to worship idols, and they are in that state: their provision comes to them, their life is good. Then he will blow into the Trumpet. And this is what he (peace be upon him) said: 'The Hour will not stand upon anyone saying: Allah, Allah.' As for at the end of time when the ummah is in general upon obedience and faith, it is not far that they are better before Allah and greater in reward, by virtue of their submission and faith with absence from witnessing the descent of revelation and the appearance of miracles and the coming down of goods and blessings, and by virtue of their steadfastness upon faith and acts of obedience and sciences and knowledge, and guidance of communities with the time and the spread of evil and the decline of virtues, and the prevalence of vices, and the dominance of people of ignorance, obstinacy, evil, and corruption. And this does not negate the goodness of the first centuries and those who follow them by the abundance of acts of obedience and worship, purity of beliefs, sincerity of intentions, and proximity of the covenant with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions, and similar things, according to what he (peace be upon him) said: 'The best of generations is the generation in which I am, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then lying will spread.'
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector points to hadiths suggesting the end-time ummah is evil, including the rain hadith which states that the beginning and end of the ummah are comparable. The author answers by distinguishing two periods: (1) the extreme end of time when belief is removed (after Jesus kills the Dajjal, a cold wind takes believers, only evil people remain worshipping idols), and (2) the general end time when the ummah is still upon faith. The manifest evil applies only to the first period. In the second period, the later generation can be superior in reward because they believe without witnessing miracles, remain steadfast despite widespread corruption, and guide others. The author then reconciles this with the hadith about the best generations (the Prophet's generation and the next two), stating that the superiority of the earlier generations is in quantity of worship and purity, not contradicting the later generation's merit under their unique circumstances.

Key Terms

الدجال

القيامة
الخيرية
القرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the later generation is universally evil; the author clarifies this is only at the extreme end.
Correction: The end-time ummah is not evil in general; evil is confined to the extreme nearness of the Hour when believers are taken away.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when does the manifest evil of the end-time ummah apply?
A) At all times of the end
B) Only at the extreme nearness of the Hour when belief is removed
C) Only during the time of the Dajjal
D) It does not apply at all

Key Takeaway
The manifest evil of the end-time ummah applies only at the extreme nearness of the Hour, not to the general end time when the ummah is still upon faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You live in a time when corruption and disbelief are widespread. The author says that believers in such times can be greater in reward because they hold onto faith without seeing miracles. ?
The hadith says that before the Hour, only the worst people remain, and they worship idols. If you were alive at that extreme end, would you be among those who have already been taken by the cold wind? What does your current faith say about your readiness to be seized by that wind?
?

And what does it demand from you now, in your own life, to live up to the potential of being a believer in the end times?

Reply to the Objection of the Hour's Delay
Objection and answer about the Hour's nearness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author reconciles the apparent delay of the Hour with hadiths indicating its nearness, by distinguishing between metaphorical nearness and the minor resurrection.

Core Idea
The 'nearness' of the Hour is either metaphorical or refers to death, not the final Hour.

A common objection against belief in the Hour is that the Prophet (ﷺ) said it would come very soon, yet centuries have passed. In this passage, the author addresses this objection head-on, offering two key interpretive moves. First, he reinterprets the 'nearness' as relative to all past time. Second, he argues that the hadith about a hundred years refers to the minor resurrection—death—not the final, major resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector cites hadiths like 'I and the Hour were sent like these two fingers' and 'no soul will live a hundred years' to argue that the Hour should have come long ago.
Notice the objector uses two different hadiths to press the point.
2
Understand the first part of the answer
The author says the nearness is like the closeness of two fingers, but only relative to the entire past of the world, not to the immediate present. This is a metaphorical interpretation.
The author does not deny the hadith's wording; he reinterprets its meaning.
3
Understand the second part of the answer
The author explains that the hadith about a hundred years refers to the minor resurrection (death), as supported by the Prophet's saying 'Whoever dies, his resurrection has come to pass' and the incident with the Bedouins.
This distinction is crucial: the 'hour' can mean death, not the final Day.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
The author deflects the objection by showing that the hadiths do not contradict the delay of the major resurrection. The passage cuts off while introducing the major resurrection, but the answer is complete.

If it is said: Hadiths about the nearness of the Hour indicate that it will come soon, like his saying: 'I and the Hour were sent like these two' meaning the index and middle fingers. Rather, they indicate that it will be before a hundred years, like his saying: 'They ask me about the Hour, and its knowledge is only with Allah, and I swear by Allah that there is no living soul on earth upon whom a hundred years will come.' And his saying: 'A hundred years will not come while there is a living soul on earth.' And we today have approached eight hundred years, and none of those signs have appeared. We say: The intended meaning is that the nearness of the Hour relative to future time in addition to what has passed is like the nearness between the two fingers, or like the superiority of the middle finger over the index finger. And the hadith of a hundred years is only about the minor resurrection, referred to by his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever dies, his resurrection has come to pass.' And his saying to a group of Bedouins who asked him about the Hour, and he pointed to the youngest among them: 'If this one lives, old age will not overtake him until your hour comes to pass upon you.' The discussion is only about the major resurrection, which is
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector notes that hadiths suggest the Hour would come very soon (like between two fingers) and within a hundred years of the Prophet's time, yet many centuries have passed without any signs. The author answers by reinterpreting the nearness: it is relative to the entire past of the world, not to the immediate present. The hadith about a hundred years refers not to the final Hour but to the 'minor resurrection' (al-qiyamah al-sughra), which is death. He supports this with the Prophet's statement 'Whoever dies, his resurrection has come to pass' and the incident where he told Bedouins that their 'hour' (i.e., death) would come before the youngest among them grew old. The passage cuts off while stating that the discussion is about the major resurrection (al-qiyamah al-kubra), implying that the hundred-year hadith does not apply to it.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith about the Hour being within a hundred years refers to the final, major resurrection.
Correction: The author clarifies that it refers to the minor resurrection (death) of that generation, not the final Hour.

Will you seek a deeper understanding (ta'wil) with humility, as this lesson demonstrates, or will you let that struggle weaken your faith?

The Objection of the Nearness of the Hour
Objection and first part of the answer on relative nearness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the common objection raised from hadiths about the imminent Hour and the first part of the answer: that the nearness is relative to all past time.

Core Idea
The Hour's nearness is relative to all past time, not a fixed short period.

Many hadiths seem to say the Hour will occur within a hundred years of the Prophet's time. When centuries passed, some questioned these hadiths. This lesson presents the objection and the answer that the nearness is like the closeness of two fingers compared to the entire span of history.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and hadiths
Read the passage carefully. Identify the objector's claim and the three hadiths cited: the finger analogy, the hundred-year oath, and the declaration that no soul will live a hundred years.
Notice that the objector uses these to argue that the Hour should have already occurred.
2
Understand the objector's conclusion
The objector notes that eight hundred years have passed without the signs appearing. This creates an apparent contradiction with the hadiths.
3
Study the answer: relative nearness
The author explains that 'nearness' is relative: compared to the entire past of humanity, the remaining time is as close as the gap between two fingers. It does not mean a literal few years.
Think of the analogy: the remaining time is short only when measured against the vast past.
4
Reflect on the significance
This interpretation preserves the truth of the hadith while explaining the delay. The Hour is indeed near relative to the whole of history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : في أحاديث قرب الساعة ما يشعر بأنها تقوم قريباً، كقوله : بعثت أنا والساعة كهاتين يعني السبابة والوسطى . بل على أنها تكون قبل مائة سنة ، كقوله : «يسألونني عن الساعة ، وإنما علمها عند الله ، وأقسم بالله ما على الأرض من نفس منفوسة يأتي عليها مائة سنة . وكقوله : «لا يأتي مائة سنة وعلى الأرض نفس منفوسة وها نحن اليوم شارفنا ثمان مائة سنة، ولم يظهر شيء من تلك العلامات .
قلنا : المراد أن قرب الساعة من مستقبل الزمان بالإضافة إلى ما مضى كقرب ما بين الإصبعين ، أو كفضل الوسطى على السبابة. وحديث مائة سنة إنما هو في القيامة الصغرى المشار إليها بقوله من مات فقد قامت قيامته، وقوله لجمع من الأعراب سألوه عن الساعة، وقد أشار الى أصغرهم : إن يعش هذا لا يدركه الهرم حتى يقوم عليكم ساعتكم وإنما الكلام في القيامة الكبرى التي هي حشر الكل وسوقهم إلى المحشر، على أن الحديث ليس على عمومه لبقاء الخضر، بل إلياس أيضاً، على ما ذهب إليه العظماء من العلماء من أن أربعة من الأنبياء في زمرة الأحياء الخضر وإلياس في الأرض، وعيسى وإدريس في السماء عليهم الصلاة والسلام .
For it is said: In the hadiths about the nearness of the Hour, there is an indication that it will occur soon, such as his saying: 'I and the Hour were sent like these two' meaning the index and middle fingers. Rather, that it will occur before a hundred years, such as his saying: 'They ask me about the Hour, but its knowledge is only with Allah, and I swear by Allah that there is no living soul on earth upon whom a hundred years will pass.' And his saying: 'A hundred years will not pass while there is a living soul on earth.' And today we have approached eight hundred years, and none of those signs have appeared. We say: The intended meaning is that the nearness of the Hour relative to future time, in addition to what has passed, is like the closeness between the two fingers, or like the superiority of the middle finger over the index finger. The hadith of a hundred years refers to the minor resurrection, indicated by his saying: 'Whoever dies, his resurrection has occurred,' and his saying to a group of Bedouins who asked him about the Hour, pointing to the youngest of them: 'If this one lives, he will not reach old age until your hour comes upon you.' The discussion concerns the major resurrection, which is the gathering of all and their driving to the place of assembly, although the hadith is not general due to the survival of al-Khidr, and also Ilyas, according to what the great scholars have held: that four of the prophets are among the living: al-Khidr and Ilyas on earth, and Jesus and Idris in heaven, peace be upon them all.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer (qaalū ... qulnā) format. The objector points to several hadiths that seem to indicate the Hour will occur very soon after the Prophet's time—within a hundred years—and observes that many centuries have passed without fulfillment. The answer provides a multi-layered interpretation: (1) The 'nearness' is relative: compared to the entire span of past history, the remaining time is short, like the gap between two fingers. (2) The hadith about 'a hundred years' refers to the minor resurrection (the death of that generation), not the major resurrection. (3) The major resurrection is the true gathering on the Day of Judgment, and its timing remains unknown. (4) The hadith about 'no soul on earth after a hundred years' is not universal because prophets like al-Khidr and Ilyas are still alive, as held by many scholars. This preserves the literal meaning of the hadith while reconciling it with the passage of time.

Key Terms
الساعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadiths guarantee the Hour within a century of the Prophet, leading to doubt when it did not occur.
Correction: The nearness is relative to all of past history, not a fixed short period.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the hadith about the two fingers (index and middle) regarding the nearness of the Hour?
A) It means the Hour will occur literally soon, within a few generations.
B) It means the nearness of the Hour is relative to the entire past, like the small gap between two fingers.
C) It means the Hour will occur exactly when the middle finger is longer than the index.
D) It means the Prophet was uncertain about the timing.

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction in hadiths about the Hour's timing is resolved by understanding 'nearness' as relative to the vast past.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that God's promises are delayed? How does this lesson challenge your impatience with divine timing? What would change if you truly believed that what seems far is actually near relative to eternity?
?
When you read the hadith about the Hour being near, do you live with urgency or complacency? Which mindset does this lesson actually demand, and are you willing to adopt it starting today?
?
If you were an early Muslim, would you have doubted the hadith when centuries passed? What does your answer reveal about your trust in the Prophet's words, and what step will you take to strengthen that trust?

Minor and Major Resurrection and the Survival of Prophets
Second part of the answer: distinction of resurrections and survival of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the minor and major resurrection and the exception of living prophets, which explains the hadith about no soul after a hundred years.

Core Idea
The hundred-year hadith refers to the minor resurrection (death), and the major resurrection remains unknown.

The objector's second point uses a hadith that says no living soul will remain after a hundred years. The author answers by distinguishing between the minor resurrection (death of that generation) and the major resurrection (final gathering), and also notes that prophets like al-Khidr and Ilyas are still alive, so the hadith is not universal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on minor and major resurrection
Read the passage carefully. Notice how the author reinterprets the hundred-year hadith as referring to the minor resurrection—the death of that generation—not the final Hour.
The minor resurrection is the death of an individual, as in 'Whoever dies, his resurrection has occurred.'
2
Examine the evidence from the Bedouin
The author cites the Prophet's statement to a group of Bedouins: pointing to the youngest, he said that his 'hour' (i.e., his death) would come before he reached old age. This illustrates the concept of minor resurrection.
This shows that 'Saturday' can refer to personal death, not the global Hour.
3
Understand the exclusion of prophets
The author notes that the hadith about no soul after a hundred years is not universal because prophets like al-Khidr and Ilyas are still alive on earth, while Jesus and Idris are alive in heaven, according to many scholars.
This preserves the literal meaning of the hadith while accommodating living prophets.
4
Reflect on the overall reconciliation
The passage shows that the apparent contradiction is resolved by recognizing that the hadith does not refer to the major resurrection, and that it has exceptions. The major resurrection remains hidden in Allah's knowledge.
